            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             9. Scottie Pippen: NBA Jam
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:400px">
            <img alt="9. Scottie Pippen: NBA Jam" data-defer-src="http://cdn.bleacherreport.net/images_root/slides/photos/000/434/478/Nba-jam-dunk_crop_400x254.png?1286568854" height="254" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="400"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            While Michael Jordan was hitting fly balls instead of three pointers in 1993, Scottie Pippen was given the chance to ascend to "His Airness'" throne, and show that he did not need M.J. to win a title. Pippen failed to do so, but he secured a title of other sorts: the best player in NBA Jam.
           </p>
           <p>
            Considering NBA Jam is arguably the best basketball game of all time, it is no petty title. Pippen was unstoppable with the ball in his hands. He was deadly from behind the arc, and was one of few players who rarely lost the ball.
           </p>
           <p>
            Had Jordan been in the game, he and Pippen would have teamed up to create the best video game basketball team of all time. Instead, that honor might soon go to the Miami Heat in NBA 2K11.
           </p>
           <p>
           </p>
           <p>
            <object height="385" width="480">
             <param name="movie" value="http://www.youtube.com/v/hncvGSwO1-E?fs=1&amp;hl=en_US">
             </param>
             <param name="allowFullScreen" value="true">
             </param>
             <param name="allowscriptaccess" value="always">
             </param>
             <embed height="385" src="http://www.youtube.com/v/hncvGSwO1-E?fs=1&amp;hl=en_US" type="application/x-shockwave-flash" width="480">
             </embed>
            </object>
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             8. Randy Moss: NFL 2k3
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:350px">
            <img alt="8. Randy Moss: NFL 2k3" data-defer-src="http://cdn.bleacherreport.net/images_root/slides/photos/000/438/107/mossNFL_display_image_crop_350x306.jpg?1286829223" height="306" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="350"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            It's tough to distinguish who was more dominant: real life Randy Moss or NFL 2K Randy Moss.
           </p>
           <p>
            Both were virtual locks to reel in any deep pass, but considering virtual Randy Moss was capable of hauling in about six per game, he gets the edge.
           </p>
           <p>
            Moss received some of the ole "Cover Boy Treatment," and he was literally unstoppable.
           </p>
           <p>
           </p>
           <p>
            <object height="385" width="480">
             <param name="movie" value="http://www.youtube.com/v/9Mf1dNeYly0?fs=1&amp;hl=en_US">
             </param>
             <param name="allowFullScreen" value="true">
             </param>
             <param name="allowscriptaccess" value="always">
             </param>
             <embed height="385" src="http://www.youtube.com/v/9Mf1dNeYly0?fs=1&amp;hl=en_US" type="application/x-shockwave-flash" width="480">
             </embed>
            </object>
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-45 cf display-none " data-page="45">
          <header class="article_page-header">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             7. Ken Griffey Jr.: Any of the Ken Griffey Jr. Games
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:350px">
            <img alt="7. Ken Griffey Jr.: Any of the Ken Griffey Jr. Games " data-defer-src="http://cdn.bleacherreport.net/images_root/slides/photos/000/438/451/kengriffey_display_image_crop_350x263.jpg?1286832424" height="263" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="350"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Ken Griffey Jr. set countless records during the duration of his storied 19 year career. But which one is the most impressive? How about earning starring roles in four video games?
           </p>
           <p>
            Griffey not only graced the cover of two Super Nintendo, and two N64 baseball games, but all four were named after Junior. In Ken Griffey Jr. Presents Major League Baseball, Ken Griffey, Jr.'s Winning Run, Major League Baseball featuring Ken Griffey, Jr., and Ken Griffey, Jr.'s Slugfest, Griffey was a juggernaut. He could blast a home run every single time he came up to bat, especially if he was being controlled by a human.
           </p>
           <p>
            He had amazing speed, and could easily swat 70 home runs in a season.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-46 cf display-none " data-page="46">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             6. Sunday Tiger Woods: Tiger Woods PGA Tour
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:570px">
            <img alt="6. Sunday Tiger Woods: Tiger Woods PGA Tour" data-defer-src="http://cdn.bleacherreport.net/images_root/slides/photos/000/434/412/Tiger-Woods-PGA-Tour-10-for-the-Wii-Review_crop_570x300.jpg?1286566214" height="300" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="570"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Before his life imploded, Tiger Woods was virtually unbeatable on the golf course. He was equally dangerous on the virtual golf course. Not only was Tiger on the cover EA Sports' annual golf game, but the game is actually named after the golfer.
           </p>
           <p>
            So, naturally, he is nothing short of a juggernaut. If you were lucky enough to make the cut and stay in contention on Sunday, good luck fending off "Sunday" Tiger Woods. "Sunday" Tiger is essentially Tiger Woods 2.0, and if you wanted to beat him, you better play the best round of virtual golf of your life.
           </p>
           <p>
            <object height="385" width="480">
             <param name="movie" value="http://www.youtube.com/v/FZ1st1Vw2kY?fs=1&amp;hl=en_US">
             </param>
             <param name="allowFullScreen" value="true">
             </param>
             <param name="allowscriptaccess" value="always">
             </param>
             <embed src="http://www.youtube.com/v/FZ1st1Vw2kY?fs=1&amp;hl=en_US" type="application/x-shockwave-flash">
             </embed>
            </object>
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-47 cf display-none " data-page="47">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             5. Lawrence Taylor: Tecmo Bowl
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:280px">
            <img alt="5. Lawrence Taylor: Tecmo Bowl" data-defer-src="http://cdn.bleacherreport.net/images_root/slides/photos/000/438/401/Lawrence-Taylor-tale_crop_280x230.jpg?1286829762" height="230" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="280"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            If you have noticed any trends on this list, one might be the absence of defenders. The reasoning behind this is, quite simply, defenders rarely steal the spotlight in video games. Great video game linebackers, defensemen, and shortstops are vital to creating a successful video game dynasty, but rarely do they create highlight reels.
           </p>
           <p>
            That is why Lawrence Taylor's Tecmo Bowl character is so special. He caused chaos and wreaked havoc on offenses, and he was the only player capable of putting a lid on Walter Payton, Christian Okoye, and Bo Jackson.
           </p>
           <p>
            He flew around the field, sideline to sideline, chasing down any player regardless of their speed. One could make a compelling case that L.T. deserves the top spot on this list, and it would be tough to argue.
           </p>
           <p>
            <object height="385" width="480">
             <param name="movie" value="http://www.youtube.com/v/B8b7_J6k-cE?fs=1&amp;hl=en_US">
             </param>
             <param name="allowFullScreen" value="true">
             </param>
             <param name="allowscriptaccess" value="always">
             </param>
             <embed height="385" src="http://www.youtube.com/v/B8b7_J6k-cE?fs=1&amp;hl=en_US" type="application/x-shockwave-flash" width="480">
             </embed>
            </object>
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-48 cf display-none " data-page="48">
          <header class="article_page-header">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             4. Jeremy Roenick: NHL 94
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:350px">
            <img alt="4. Jeremy Roenick: NHL 94" data-defer-src="http://cdn.bleacherreport.net/images_root/slides/photos/000/434/473/nhlgroenick300_display_image_crop_350x233.jpg?1286568415" height="233" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="350"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            The legend of Jeremy Roenick's NHL '94 character was built largely in thanks to a scene in the 1996 comedy "Swingers" where Vince Vaughn dominates Patrick Van Horn in a game of NHL '94. Roenick is spotted skating circles around Van Horn's team, burying every shot he takes into the back of the net.
           </p>
           <p>
            Roenick's '94 video game character can only be compared to some of these Tecmo Bowl football players. He could skate around the ice without losing the puck, and then easily whip a no look backhander behind the opposing goaltender.
           </p>
           <p>
            Hence, Jeremy Roenick takes the honor of most dominant video game hockey player of all time.
           </p>
           <p>
           </p>
           <p>
            <object height="385" width="480">
             <param name="movie" value="http://www.youtube.com/v/03JgYUDtHkE?fs=1&amp;hl=en_US">
             </param>
             <param name="allowFullScreen" value="true">
             </param>
             <param name="allowscriptaccess" value="always">
             </param>
             <embed height="385" src="http://www.youtube.com/v/03JgYUDtHkE?fs=1&amp;hl=en_US" type="application/x-shockwave-flash" width="480">
             </embed>
            </object>
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-49 cf display-none " data-page="49">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             3. Michael Vick: Madden 2004
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:275px">
            <img alt="3. Michael Vick: Madden 2004" data-defer-src="http://cdn.bleacherreport.net/images_root/slides/photos/000/439/247/vick_madden_2_crop_275x200.jpg?1286854970" height="200" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="275"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            You could drop back 50 yards and still scramble your way into the end zone, or you could drop back 50 yards and sling a rocket-pass 80 yards down field to an open receiver. Basically, if you were playing with Michael Vick in Madden '04 (or '07), anything was possible.
           </p>
           <p>
            Vick's Madden character has reached legend status, and if he finishes his career without a Super Bowl ring, it's plausible to believe that his video game character career will carry as much notoriety as his actual career.
           </p>
           <p>
            The Atlanta Falcons teams featuring Vick led to countless arguments between you and your friends before you finally just outlawed the team all together. That being said, it was possible to stop Vick. If you played a strict QB Contain defense and forced him to throw, you could at least limit the damage.
           </p>
           <p>
            By the way, Falcons receiver Brian Finneran never enjoyed so much success on the NFL stage as he did in Madden alongside Vick. For one reason or another, Finneran was just always open.
           </p>
           <p>
            <object height="385" width="480">
             <param name="movie" value="http://www.youtube.com/v/YdhLCpEZkLo?fs=1&amp;hl=en_US">
             </param>
             <param name="allowFullScreen" value="true">
             </param>
             <param name="allowscriptaccess" value="always">
             </param>
             <embed height="385" src="http://www.youtube.com/v/YdhLCpEZkLo?fs=1&amp;hl=en_US" type="application/x-shockwave-flash" width="480">
             </embed>
            </object>
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             2. Mike Tyson: Mike Tyson's Punch Out
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:350px">
            <img alt="2. Mike Tyson: Mike Tyson's Punch Out" data-defer-src="http://cdn.bleacherreport.net/images_root/slides/photos/000/438/421/tyson_display_image_crop_350x305.jpg?1286831550" height="305" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="350"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            You could not beat him.
           </p>
           <p>
            Few saw Tyson actually witnessed Tyson fall to the mat, and those who claim they knocked out the champ were always hammered with doubt and skepticism. There was probably one kid on your street who claims to have defeated Tyson, but his words became that of folklore.
           </p>
           <p>
            However, it was possible to beat Iron Mike. All the evidence you need is right here in this video. So, for those of you who don't believe it was possible, or want to pull out the Nintendo for another go around, have a watch.
           </p>
           <p>
           </p>
           <p>
            <object height="385" width="480">
             <param name="movie" value="http://www.youtube.com/v/hu69QEHhvNo?fs=1&amp;hl=en_US">
             </param>
             <param name="allowFullScreen" value="true">
             </param>
             <param name="allowscriptaccess" value="always">
             </param>
             <embed height="385" src="http://www.youtube.com/v/hu69QEHhvNo?fs=1&amp;hl=en_US" type="application/x-shockwave-flash" width="480">
             </embed>
            </object>
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             1. Bo Jackson: Tecmo Super Bowl
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:445px">
            <img alt="1. Bo Jackson: Tecmo Super Bowl" data-defer-src="http://cdn.bleacherreport.net/images_root/slides/photos/000/434/405/bo_jackson_tecmo_crop_445x307.jpg?1286565770" height="307" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="445"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            Tecmo Bowl Bo Jackson is everything we love and everything we hate about video games.
           </p>
           <p>
            He was untouchable and unbeatable. He was a juggernaut, and his video game character has reached epic and godly status.
           </p>
           <p>
            Few other video game athletes dominated their games like Bo did. He could literally run circles around defenders, turn a 100 yard run into a 400 yard run, and bulldoze any defender who dared stand in his path.
           </p>
           <p>
            As much as you loved playing with him and despised playing against him, the days of Bo Jackson video game characters have come to a close. Thankfully, video evidence of his legendary prowess will never perish.
           </p>
           <p>
            <object height="385" width="480">
             <param name="movie" value="http://www.youtube.com/v/8PBvOxicz-0?fs=1&amp;hl=en_US">
             </param>
             <param name="allowFullScreen" value="true">
             </param>
             <param name="allowscriptaccess" value="always">
             </param>
             <embed height="385" src="http://www.youtube.com/v/8PBvOxicz-0?fs=1&amp;hl=en_US" type="application/x-shockwave-flash" width="480">
             </embed>
            </object>
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

  		gads.src = (useSSL ? 'https:' : 'http:') + '//www.googletagservices.com/tag/js/gpt.js';
  		var node = document.getElementsByTagName('head')[0];
  		node.parentNode.insertBefore(gads, node);
    }
	})();
